**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

Summarizing:

You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Daily Intelligence Briefing for Congressional Leadership**
**Date: July [XX], 2025**

**AREA 1: ECONOMIC POLICY & PERFORMANCE**

**Topic 1.1: Inflation, Tariffs, and Consumer Prices**
Economic reports for June 2025 indicate an acceleration in U.S. inflation. Official data shows a 2.7% annual rate [1], marking the highest level in four months [2]. A strong consensus is emerging across multiple analyses that directly links this inflationary pressure to the administration's tariff policies. Reports state that the effects of the tariffs are now beginning to "show in prices" [3] and are starting to "bite" American consumers [4]. The connection is so clear that some analyses explicitly declare, "It’s Official: Trump’s Tariffs Are Driving Up Inflation" [5]. This body of reporting presents a unified conclusion: the administration's trade strategy is a primary and observable driver of rising costs for American households.

**References:**
[1] Inflation picks up again in June, rising at 2.7% annual rate, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/15/cpi-inflation-report-june-2025.html

[2] US inflation rebounded in June to highest level in four months, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/15/economy/us-cpi-consumer-price-index-inflation-june

**Topic 1.2: Federal Budget and Fiscal Policy**
The administration's fiscal agenda faces significant legislative examination, particularly from within the Republican party. GOP lawmakers are reportedly considering changes to President Trump's specific request for $9.4 billion in spending cuts. This development signals potential difficulties for the White House ahead of a critical test vote, suggesting the proposal may not pass without modification [1]. On a related fiscal front, a new analysis of recently enacted tax and spending legislation projects a significant adverse effect on energy costs. According to a report from NPR, consumers and businesses should expect power prices to "soar" as a direct consequence of the new law, creating a new economic pressure point [2].

**References:**
[1] Republicans are considering changes to Trump’s request for $9.4 billion in spending cuts, signaling potential difficulties ahead of an important test vote., https://apnews.com/article/trump-republicans-budget-cuts-pepfar-pbs-npr-b224d4dd5962f141b23e76a4893e0d39

**Topic 1.3: Federal Reserve and Monetary Policy**
The leadership of the Federal Reserve has become a center of public and political friction. Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent, a key economic official in the administration, publicly stated his belief that Chair Jerome H. Powell "Should Leave the Fed Board in May," according to a Bloomberg report [1]. This direct call for a leadership change at the central bank was met with stark warnings from economic commentators. An opinion piece in The New York Times framed the issue in dramatic terms, cautioning against the move with the headline, "If You Like 35 Percent Inflation, Go Ahead, Fire the Fed Chair" [2]. The public debate highlights a fundamental conflict over the independence of the central bank and the potential for political pressure to influence monetary policy.

**References:**

**Topic 1.4: International Trade and Supply Chains**
The administration's tariff-centric trade policy is generating significant repercussions in both diplomatic negotiations and key industries. Diplomatically, Canadian Prime Minister Mark Carney has publicly acknowledged that securing a U.S. trade deal without the inclusion of at least some tariffs is now "unlikely" [1, 2]. This signals a strategic realignment from a key trading partner. The President's "tariff letters" are reportedly causing "a stir among world leaders," indicating widespread international concern [3]. The impact is also being felt directly in supply chains. An industry lobby reports that American meatpackers are rethinking beef export strategies to the United States as a direct result of the new duties, a tangible consequence for the agricultural sector [4].

**AREA 2: THE EPSTEIN CASE: POLITICAL AND LEGAL FALLOUT**

**Topic 2.1: Congressional Action on Release of Files**
A high-profile legislative effort to compel the public release of the Jeffrey Epstein files was defeated in the House of Representatives. Multiple reports confirm that House Republicans blocked the measure during a procedural vote, preventing it from moving forward [1]. The official roll call, published as Vote 149 on page 5 of the House Rules Committee record, identifies the members who voted against the release [2]. Following the vote, Newsweek published what it presented as the "Full list of Republicans who blocked Epstein files vote" [3]. Representative Ro Khanna, the bill's sponsor, questioned the motives for the block, vowing to continue the fight for transparency. He is quoted: "We won't stop until the files are released... This may have been our first attempt, but the public will not be gaslit" [4].

"This may have been our first attempt, but the public will not be gaslit. We will keep fighting for transparency.", https://www.commondreams.org/news/gop-blocks-epstein-files-release

**Topic 2.2: Partisan Conflict and Internal GOP Disputes**
The failure to release the Epstein files has escalated into a sharply partisan conflict while exposing deep fissures within the Republican party. Leadership-level Democrats in both chambers, including Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries, have publicly accused Republicans of either having "Lied About Epstein Evidence or Are Now Covering It Up" [1]. This external pressure is compounded by significant internal strife. One analysis describes the situation as an "Epstein Civil War" being waged among five distinct "MAGA Factions" [2]. This infighting is further evidenced by reports of Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene going "to war with Trump" over his handling of the files [3]. The bitterness is palpable, with one report noting a GOP Congressman is now mocking "MAGA Over Epstein Files" after a pro-Trump super PAC spent $1.8 million in a failed attempt to unseat him [4].

### 3.2. U.S.-China Relations and Technology Policy
A significant shift in U.S. technology export policy concerning China appears imminent. Following a direct meeting between President Trump and the CEO of Nvidia, the Associated Press reported that the sale of advanced AI chips to China is "back on" [1]. This development represents a potential reversal of prior policy that restricted high-tech exports to a strategic competitor. The move comes as Senate Democrats publicly assert that the administration's broader policies are actively hurting America's ability to effectively compete with China on the global stage, indicating a sharp divergence between administration actions and certain congressional viewpoints on national strategy [2].

**References:**

### 3.3. U.S. Global Standing and National Security Personnel
Recent polling data indicates a troubling decline in the international standing of the United States. A new Pew Research survey reveals that "Views of the U.S. have worsened" across numerous surveyed countries, a trend that coincides with a modest improvement in global opinions of China over the same period [1, 2]. This data suggests a potential erosion of U.S. soft power. Separately, the administration's national security appointments are facing sharp criticism. In a quote reported by The Guardian, noted CIA historian Tim Weiner offered a scathing assessment, asserting that President Trump "has put national security in the hands of crackpots and fools" [3].

## 4. Domestic Policy and Governance

### 4.1. Immigration Enforcement and Detainee Conditions
The administration is escalating immigration enforcement through enhanced data sharing and policy changes affecting detainees. A ProPublica report reveals the IRS is building a "vast system" to share millions of taxpayers’ data files directly with Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) [1]. Concurrently, the administration has formally rescinded abuse protections for transgender individuals held in ICE custody, a significant policy reversal [2]. These actions coincide with severe reports about detainee welfare at a Florida immigrant jail. Activists and lawmakers allege "inhumane conditions with no due process" for hundreds of individuals [3]. After a visit, Rep. Maxwell Frost shared "ominous findings" from the site, which has been dubbed "Alligator Alcatraz" [4].

**References:**
[1] The IRS Is Building a Vast System to Share Millions of Taxpayers’ Data With ICE, https://www.propublica.org/article/trump-irs-share-tax-records-ice-dhs-deportations?utm_source=sailthru&utm_medium=email&utm_campaign=majorinvestigations&utm_content=toc

### 4.2. Healthcare and Social Services Policy
Multiple reports highlight significant administration actions creating disruptions across healthcare and social services. One report alleges a plan within the Trump administration to incinerate 500 tons of emergency food originally meant for children [1]. In healthcare, direct pressure from the administration has reportedly forced the nation's largest gender-affirming youth clinic, The Center for Transyouth Health and Development, to cease all new patient care and face a complete shutdown within weeks [2]. The downstream effects of federal fiscal policy are also coming into view. One study projects that due to Medicaid cuts, 93 nursing homes in Illinois are at risk of closing [3]. A separate study focusing on Wyoming found the same cuts are expected to shrink the state's economy by $140 million over the next five years [4].

### 4.3. Judicial Nominations and Agency Oversight
The administration's personnel selections for the judiciary and federal regulatory bodies are encountering organized opposition. A coalition of over 75 former judges has formally urged the relevant Senate committee to reject the judicial nomination of Emil Bove, signaling significant concern from the legal community [1]. Separately, a Reuters report indicates the U.S. nuclear regulator has been asking job applicants political questions during the hiring process, sparking concerns about politicized hiring practices in sensitive roles [2]. These events occur as employees within the nation's consumer financial watchdog have alleged that the agency has become "toothless under Trump" [3].

## 5. Domestic Political Landscape and Societal Tensions

### 5.1. High-Profile Political Conflicts
Partisan rhetoric is escalating through direct, personal attacks. Following a DOJ criminal referral, President Trump publicly accused Senator Adam Schiff of "mortgage fraud," calling him a "scam artist" who must be "brought to justice" [1]. The accusation centers on Senator Schiff's Maryland home, which he maintains while representing his California district [2]. This animosity extends to state-level politics, where Gavin Newsom has floated the idea of "redistricting retribution" against the Texas GOP, should they proceed with redrawing their state's electoral maps before the midterms [3].

### 5.2. Trust in Institutions and Future Elections
The erosion of public trust in government institutions is an emerging theme with direct political ramifications. Citing what she called a "profound erosion in trust," Democratic Lawmaker Rep. Marie Gluesenkamp Perez has vowed to push for systemic reform by advocating for cognitive tests as a form of mental fitness oversight for members of Congress [1]. This call for accountability resonates with broader societal concerns, including analyses that point to a growing "tide of voter mistrust" in the election process itself [2]. Against this backdrop, positioning for the 2028 presidential election is already underway, with reports indicating prominent Democrats—including "Pritzker to Newsom to Emanuel"—are already campaigning in key early voting states [3].
